I still remember vividly my first grade teacher being called out of class, then returning a few minutes later crying - something as first graders we had never seen before. She was the one who told us that President Kennedy had been shot, and that we would be going home soon. Not long afterward, the busses showed up and we were all sent home to hear the news that President Kennedy had died. As a 6 year old it was hard to fathom just how big a moment in our country's history this was, but I never forgot that day the rest of my life. C-Company and C-Battery will have a joint ceremony at 10 a.m. on Friday, August 23 and Squadron 4 will hold their ceremony at 11 a.m. on Saturday August 24. Each ceremony will include the unit activation ceremony and remarks from the Commandant of the Corps, unit commanders and former unit members. Both ceremonies will be followed by a reception inside the Sanders Corps Center for current cadets and former students. \r\n\r\nFor 137 years, the Texas A&M University Corps of Cadets has been producing leaders of character and preserving Aggie traditions. The individual units in the Corps have developed their own unique histories and traditions while maintaining a solid, united union of the Corps of Cadets.\r\n\r\nThroughout Corps history, various units have stood down for differing reasons \u2014 gone, but never forgotten \u2014 especially by their former members, eager to see their beloved units restored.\r\n\r\nIn 2012, the decision was made to reactivate two units, Squadron 1 and Company F-1. Last year, the decision was made to reactivate two additional units, Squadron 6 and Company S-2, to accommodate the steady growth of incoming students eager to be part of the storied Corps of Cadets.  There are plans to reactivate more units in the near future as the Corps continues to grow and the need to have more units increases.\r\n\r\n\u201cOver the past two years, we have reactivated four units, all of which have done well and are thriving again. With the Corps growing every year (we project almost 2,500 cadets for this fall semester, the largest in over 40 years) one priority is to ensure we have the proper place for all of them. I am very pleased to add these three additional units, C-Company and C-Battery, part of our 460-member Aggie Band, and Squadron 4, to the ranks of the Corps of Cadets as well,\u201d said Brigadier General Joe E. Ramirez, Jr. \u201979, commandant of the Corps. \u201cThey are a part of our Corps history and will be a new source of pride for our current cadets. The former cadets who were members of these units will be pleased to see their guidons once again flying on campus. "created_time": "2013-06-10T17:07:36+0000", "message": "It is with extreme sadness that I confirm the death of Lieutenant Colonel Todd Clark '94 in Afghanistan this past weekend. Todd was a Fightin' Texas Aggie Class of \u201994 and a proud member of Company B-2 in the Corps of Cadets. He had a distinguished 17-year career in the U.S. Army, most recently as a brigade-level advisor with the Army's 10th Mountain Division. Todd served three tours in Iraq and was on his second tour in Afghanistan when he was killed. In July 2010, Todd received a Purple Heart for injuries sustained by a roadside bomb in Kandahar and spent his recovery at Walter Reed, becoming deeply involved in the Wounded Warrior program. I share the sentiment left on his Facebook page by a friend that Todd was a: \"Loving Husband and Father. Great Son. Leader. Mentor. Wounded Warrior ... Our Hero. Our Friend. Our Role Model.\" A fitting description and tribute to a great man. After this last tour in Afghanistan, Todd was going to return to Aggieland in the fall to serve as Executive Officer in the Texas A&M Army ROTC program, a job he described as his \u201cdream job.\u201d The Office of the Commandant and the Corps of Cadets offer their sincere condolences to Todd\u2019s wife Shelley, his children Madison and Collin, his parents Jack and Kathleen, his fellow B-2 classmates, and his extended family and friends. Todd makes the 29th Aggie and former member of the Corps of Cadets to have died in military service since 9/11 \u2013 something we should never forget. We will provide information on funeral arrangements as they become available. May God Bless Todd and his family, and may we never forget his sacrifice for our country and our freedoms. Rest in peace, Todd.
